Budgeting and Filnancdal Management
8.    With respect to financing LODP, MFEP represents the GO(   as the borrower of IDA funds
and as the GO party to the IDA Credit Agreement. It also performs an important role with respect
to the generation of GOG's direct financing of a proportion of project costs through the budget of
MLGRD.
9.    TSC will have primary responsibility, on behalf of MLGRD, for budgeting and management
of funds provided under the terms of LGDP. Thus, TSC will: (a) facilitate approval of financing for
approved sub-projects; (b) mainain, jointly with MLGRD, a Special Account for the holding and
disbursing of IDA funds and a Project Account for the holding and disbursing of GO counterpart
fxnds, authorized signatories for which will include at teast one signature each from ISC and
MLGRD (NOTE: Adoption of this clause will be subject to any over-riding clauses regarding the
authorized procedures for maintining LGDP-related bank accounts and disbursements from those
accounts included in the GOG/IDA Credit Agreement; including the possibility of the relevant District
Assemblies holding and disbursing any financial contributions that might be provided by their own
sources); and (c) maintain financial accounts and provide periodic financial reports as required. Sub-
project accounts will be established in each of the LGDP districts finmced from the project account
operated by TSC/MLGRD. Payments to local consultants and contractors will be made from such
accounts.
Procurement and Contract Administtion
10.   TSC will have overall responsibility for supervising procurement activities and contract
administraion; with specific subordinate responsibilities involving LGSU, District Assemblies, and
relevant tender boards at district, regional, and central government levels (as required by GO0
procurement regulations). Organizational arrangements have been designed so as to conform with
IDA procurement guidelines. ITe Ghana Supply Commission (0SC) has a special role in the review
of bid documents and in bid evaluations for the procurement of goods under the waste management
sub-component of LGDP.
Techial Assistance
11. Details concerning the implementation arrangements for technical assistance are provided in
Annex 15. In summary, TSC will be responsible for providing logistical and administrative support
for TA personnel. Nevertheless, responsibflities for managing TA personnel wiUl be divided among
TSC, LGSU, and the appropriate technical or administrative departaent/unit at district level. The
broad division of responsibilities will be between TSC as the manager of the infrastructure part of the
project and the MLGRD as the manager of the institutional development and capacity-building part



-117-                               Annexl1
Page 5 of 6
In particular, LGSU will be responsible for recruiting and supervising the four TA Field Advisory
Teams finaned by the Project.
Taning
12.   Details concerning the Implementation arrangements for training are provided in Annex 10.
OJT directed towards strengdtening practical technical skills of junior staff will be provided by local
supervisors and various TA consultants within the 11 Project Districts. Training coordination at
district levels wil be the responsibility of the District Assembly personnel officer (or other specific
person assigned to this function). The person(s) responsible for organizing training will receive a
short course in Training Management (raining of Trainers) if necessary, and will also obtain advice
and assistance from consultants engaged in the project and local training institutions as needed. A-
annual training plan will be prepared in advance of each fiscal year and submitted to IDA for review
and no-objection. Preparation of the first annual training plan by each Project District will be a
condition of Effectiveness. Following the first year of the project, subsequent annual training plans
will also include an assessment of training activities carried out in the previous year. Within the cost
envelope of the project training component, training funds will be allocated to each District Assembly
on the basis of the annual taing plan. When and where additional funds for training are available
trough Government and/or other donors, this will be so noted and included in the annual training
plan.
Monitoring huplementation Performance
13.   Overall policy guidance for LGDP resides in MLGRD. In exercising that responsibility,
MLGRD will be assisted by TSC for the provision of day-to-day technical management, accounting,
and coordination. A Project Coordinating Committee (PCC), chaired by the Minister of Loca
Government and Rur Development and comprising the Chief Director of MLW RD, the heads of
TSC, LGSU, and TSU, and representatives of MFEP, NDPC, Ministry of Lands and Forestry
(NL1), OHCS, and the 11 District Assemblies will meet quarterly to review the progress of the
project. TSC will also act as the Secretariat for the PCC.
14.   On a day-to-day basis, TSC will be directly responsible for monitoring the technical and
financial performance of sub-projects for the construction or rehabilitation of roads and drains, waste
management systems and facilities, markets, and lorry parks. LGSU will be primarily responsible for
monitoring day-to-day technical and financial performance of sub-projects directed toward improved
revenue generation and management capacity at district levels, as well as the performance of all
technical assistance provided in that regard. TSU will be primarily responsible for monitoring day-to-
day technical and financial performance of training programs. The responsibilites of LGSU and TSU
for monitoring performance as specified above does not authorize either of those entities to make
binding decisions concening the implementation of the referenced components of LGDP. Iheir role
with regard to responsibilities identified in this paragraph is to advise MLGRD with respect to any
implementation problems that might be emerging.
Infrastcture Investment
15.   Detas concerning implemention arrangemes for infrastructure investments are provided in
Anmex 2. With respect to infratructure components, District Assemblies have sole responsibility for
identfying and prioritizing proposals. However, with respect to the 11 towns included in the LGDP,
idetification and prorfization of specific investments to be financed by LGDP will have been



Annea11
Page 6 of 6
completed prior to project effectiveness. Nevertheless, the on-going involvement of District
Assemblies in reviewing implementation experience and, perhaps, proposals for substituting new or
revised subprojects for previously approved investments will be necessary throughout implementation
of the project. Primary reliance will be placed on annual action-planning workshops involving the
staff from District Assemblies, MLGRD, MFEP and TSC for review and design of changes required
by experience.
16.   A flexible approach to project design and implementation is particularly relevant to LGDP
because changes can be expected in several factors likely to directly affect project implementation.
Changes in the structure of incentives within the GOG are likely independent of actions taken within
LGDP. At the same time, improved facilities, skills, and systems for planning, finance, and
management, at both Central and local government levels, will develop as a direct result of LGDP.
Iherefore, at least some proposals for changing urban infrastructure projects under LGDP are
expected to be received from District Assemblies by TSC which, in turn, would contract with private
sector consultants to assess their feasibility. When specific proposals are judged to be feasible,
private consultants would prepare detailed engineering design, under the supervision of TSC.
17.   In addition to TSC's role as outlined above, it will also be responsible for approving contracts
between the responsible District Assembly and providers for each LGDP-financed urban infrastructure
investment prior to actual disbursements for implementation of such contracts (as will the approval of
IDA where required by the GOG/IDA Credit Agreement).
DtIct Assembly Capacity-Building
18.   Details concerning arrangements for District Assembly capacity building are provided in
Annex 9. The MLGRD has overall responsibility for the strengthening of the District Assemblies.
The strengthening of Technical Departments will be accomplished through the LGSU, the engagement
of a locally recruited Municipal Engineer for each city, and training. The Municipal Engineer will be
responsible for developing and installing appropriate engineering management systems, including
programming, budgeting, project management, and infrastructure and vehicle maintenance systems.
The Engineer will be supported under the project through technical assistance. LGSU would,
however, rely upon the support of TSC for advice on drafting TORs for techical assistance and the
procurement of vehicles and equipment.

pivotal role in the Ara District Rehabilitation and Priority Works projects and has continued
as the key implementing agency of the Urban H project. TSC has accumulated the necessary
experience to manage procurement conts in accordance with Bank's Procurement
Guidelines. TSC would liaise with the DAs, GSC and other agencies. Capacity building of
DA personl in procurement and supervision will be developed by their participation in bid
evaluation and management of conactu. Table 1 shows the assigmuent of procurement
functions.

Prcweon Documentation
2.    1SC has agreed to make use of Bank sample documents for civil works,
prequaification, delivery of goods and use of consultas. Copies and diskettes of Bank
sample documents have been given to TSC. The use of standard documents shoud greatly
simplify approval of documents by the Bank for the proposed project. Preparation of techical
specifications wDI need to be handled by consulnts selected by TSC in accordance with bank
guidelines as thbis work Is too specilized for TSC to carry out in house. Other agencies,
direcdy or indity associated widh the project, were reviewed during apprais and found
generaly satisfactory for procurement activities, with the exception of the District Assemblies
(DAs), as this is their first  ence with Bank finaced operations. DAs will assist TSC
and consultants in bid evaluation and supervision of work and will thus gaim usefl direct
eperience in conOa and O&M management. In addition, DA staff wil receive TA under
the DA Capacity Building Componet under the project.
Prouemet Process Srmlining
3.    Following the Akuse m Country StratW  and Implementation Review (CSIR) on
procurement management, GO  on June 8, 1993 accepted Bank r          for
streamlining procuremt hdling. The basic principles of the new procedures are O) to place
reasonable time limits on eah major step in the procurement process following the receipt of
bids, and (U) to reduce the number of steps in the approval process. Accordingly, te time
limit for approval of bids for civil works has been fiLxed at 180 days (120 for LCB). The
Central Advisory Tender Board (CATB) would represent the final authority for approval of
award, with no further need of approval by the Ministry of Justice and the Cabinet. The
Ghana Supply Commission (GSC) which is often a botteneck and cause of delay, wil no be
direcdy involved in the Fpocment of goods but will assist TSC in the review of technical
specifications and handling of imports. For consulting contracts, the streamlined procedures
require the MFEP to accept or reject consulCY agrem     submitted to it within two weeks
of receipt of the submision
Procrement Monitoring and Review
4.    During project supervision, Bank-financed works contrs above a threshold of US$
1 million will be subject to Bank's prior review procedures. Goods contracts or packages
above US$ 200,000 will be subject to prior review, covering about 80 % of the total value of
Bank-financed goods. The review process will cover about 80% of the total works contract
value procured and 100% of the ICB contracts. Selective post review of awarded contcs
below the thrsold levels wil be caTried out on about I in 4 works contracts and I in 8
goods contracts.

REPUBLIC OF GHANA
LOCAL GOVERNMENT DEVELOPMENT PROJECT
Technical Assistance
SUMMARY
Technical assistance in the Local Government Development Project is provided for lntitutional
Strengthening and Capacity Building (see Annex 9). TA is divided into two components: (1)
improving the management capacity of District Assemblies and (2) strengthening the capacity of
central government to assist DAs. The specific TA under the two categories consists of the following
(unless Indicated, TA is provided through national consultants only):
Direct TA for 11 District Assemblies
1.    Municipal Engineering Support (160 person-months).
2.    Financial Management Support (160 person-months).
3.    District Planning and Implementation Support (160 person-months).
TA for Cen    Government Assistance to DAs
1.    Technical Services Center of MW'H (72 person-months).
2.    Policy Review of DA Revenue Mobilization, MLGRD (12 person-months).
3.    Coordinatin of Technical Assistance, MLGRD (36 person-months).
4.    Engineering Supervision by KfW of co-fimanced market and motor park component
(itrnational consultant, 30 person-months short-term).
5.    Property Revaluation, Land Valuation Board (12 person-months).
6.    Land Use Planning and Devewupment Guidance, Town and Country Planning Department,
MLGRD (22 person-months).
7.    Mappin5, Survey Department (international consultants, 9 person-months short-term).

difficult to impose on one District the obligation of provlidg office space. A total of US$120,000 is
allocated for office acco ions in the four regions over the three year TA period.

2.    FSnandal Manamt Suowrt to Districts
2.1   SeoeofWA ork
Technici assistance, through local consultants, will be provided to the District Assemblies that are
participoating in the LGDP for support and capacity-building in three areas of financial management:
(a) budgeting and accounting systems, (b) revenue Improvement action plans, and (c) property rates
billing and collecion. Consultant' advice and assistance will include the following:
Budgeting and Accounting Systems
The objectives of introducing Impioved budgedng and accounting systems in the Districts are: (a) to
enhance accountability for the efficient and effective use of resources dtrough activity-based
budgeting, (b) to provide a basis for effective monitoring of actual vs. projected revenues and
expenditures, (c) to permit assessment of the cost-effectiveness of activities, and (d) where feasible, to
improve the efficiency of budget preparation and reporting through computeatio.
1.    Assess work done under the Urban II project on the development, implantation, and
utilization of improved budgeting and accounting systems for local government. Evaluate
suitability of the improved systems, formats, and procedures developed under Urban 11 for
application to the LGDP DAs.
2.    Based to the extnt possible on the work done under the Urban 11 project, develop an activity-
based budget and accounting system that can be Implanted In the Districts.
3.    Assess capability of LODP District Assemblies to utilize computer-based budget and
accounting systems.
4.    Prepare a work plan and schedule for implandng the new systems in the DAs.

5.    Ply Reew of District Assembly Revenue Mobilization
5.1   Scope of Work (see Annex 5. Appendix 4)
Ihe pupose of this component is to assist the Govemment of Ghana to review the current allocation
of revenue sources between central government and District Assemblies with the view to revising the
current allocation of revenue-raising authority consistent with established decentraization policy.



-139-                              An= is
Page 10 of 14
Presently, local govermments act largely as agents of central government rather than exercising
significant discretionary authority as envisaged in Law 207 and the new Constitution. One of the
ways in which this inconsistency is manifested is in the current central-local allocation of authority
over revenue collection and utilization. The Government is aware that this situation bampers its
decentralization policy objectives and is drafting changes in its financial management systems which
are expected to achieve more consistency.
LGDP cannot support a comprehensive program in this area, but it will provide technical assistance
for a number of specific activities which are intended to help sustain the project's benefits. In
addition, it is expected that these interventions will contribute to improved local government
performance in most sectors.
MLGRD would collaborate with the Finance Conunittee of Parliament to create a Working Group on
the Allocation of Revenue Sources. Technical assistance will be provided to the Working Group for
the following:
1.    Conduct a comprehensive review of the current allocation of revenue sources among levels of
government.
2.    Conduct one or more action planning workshops to identify key issues, problems and
alternative solutions.
3.    Analyze the financial and institutional impacts of the various alternatives proposed.
4.    Conduct a further workshop to assess the alternative impacts and take decisions on
recommended allocations of authority for revenue-raising and utilization.
S.    Submit recommendations to the appropriate authorities.

6.    Coordinaon or Technical Asistan
6.1   Sce of WQrk
Technical assistance to the Districts in financial management (Section 2 above) and planning (Section
3 above) will be supervised by MLGRD through its Local Government Support Unit (LGSU).
Technical assistance in municipal engineering (Section I above) will be supervised by the Technical
Services Center. To ensure that the overall capacity-building effort is managed in a coordinated way,
the LGSU will receive support from one national consultant, who will be the project's Technical
Assistance Adviser (TAA). ITis person will be attached to LOSU on a full-time basis for 36 monts.
His/her functions will be:
1.    Serve as Team Leader for the overall technical assistance program of LGDP.
2.    Prepare anusal work plans for coordination of the overall technical assistance program.
3.    Assist in implementing the quarterly monitoring and reporting system for LGDP.
4.    Ensure that the consultants working with the DAs are provided with the necessary, up-to-date
guidance on Government policies and regulations relevant to their fields of activity.
5.    Provide technical advice, within his/her areas of competence, to guide the various technical
assistance efforts.
6.    Alert MLGRD, TSC, and the World Bank to issues and problems requiring attention, and
assist in follow-up.
In addition to the overall supervision provided by the TAA, day-to-day coordination of each of the
four field teams (see Sections 1,2 and 3 above) will be achieved through the designation of one of the
three field advisers on each team as Field Team Leader (FMl). All field team members will report to
their FTL, and the FTLs will report to the TAA.

GHANA
LOCAL GOVERNMENT DEVYFLOPMENT PROJECT
(Urban 111)
MEMORANDUM of UNDERSTANDING:
ROLE of TSC
Purpose
1.    This Memorandum of Understanding sets forth the agreement of the Ministry of Works
and Housing (MWH), the Ministry of Local Government and Rural Development (MLGRD) and
the Technical Services Centre of MWH (TSC) with respect to the role of TSC in the
implementation of the Local Government Development Project (LGDP) and its relationship to
MLGRD in that regard. It is understood that the relationships specified below pertain solely to
responsibilities of TSC with respect to the implementation of the LGDP. With respect to any
and aUl other responsiilities of TSC, the normal relationship between TSC as a unit of MWH,
and MWH, remains as it was prior to the effectiveness of LGDP.
Technical Management, Accounting, and Coordination
2.    Ministry of Local Govenment and Rural Development.   With respect to
implementation of the LGDP, the MLGRD is the designated Sector Ministry responsible.
Therefore, with respect to the Areas of Responsibility specified below, t' e TSC acts on behalf,
of the MLGRD. Reporting by the TSC with respect to LGDP shall be direct to the Chief
Director MLGRD.
3.    Ministry of Works and Housing. With specific respect to TSC's implementation
responsibilities under the tenrs of LGDP, and specifically limited to those specific responsibilities
of TSC, MWH shall ensure that TSC performs the role assigned to it under the project.
4.    Role of District Assemblies. As specified in paragraphs 2-3 above, TSC acts on behalf
of MLGRD  as the responsible Sector Ministry.  Nevertheless, in the exercise of its
responsibilities, TSC shall be mindful that the LGDF !rn among its objectives improved capacity
of District Assemblies to exercise specific responsibilities mandated by the Constitution of the
Fourth Republic and PNDC Law No. 207. Such responsibilities include making decisions
regarding investments, and/or operating and maintaining such investments, with respect to waste
management, markets and lorry parks, and urban streets and drains. Therefore, it can be
expected that the Credit Agreement for IDA financing of LGDP will specify roles and
responsibilities of District Assemblies for implementation of specific aspects of that project. The
terms of this Memorandum of Understanding shall be subordinate to any clauses in the IDAJGOG
Credit Agreement which govern the roles and responsibilities of the District Assemblies and
relationships among the District Assemblies, TSC, MLGRD, and/or MWH. In any event, TSC
views its role as being supportive of, and responsive to, the District Assemblies included in the
scope of the LGDP and hereby commits itself to ensure effective consultation with District
Assemblies on all significant matters for which it is assigned responsibility on behalf of MLGRD.
5.    Resolution of Disputes. In the event that disputes arise among MLGRD, MWH, and/or
TSC concerning the repository of authority to make any specific decision, take any action, or
require any specific information, the parties shall meet within seven (7) days of the dispute being
made known to any one of the parties and shall seek mutual agreement as to the appropriate roles



Anne* 18
-161-                                  Page 2 of 4
of the parties with respect to the specific dispute. Such resolution of disputes shall be guided by,
and be in conformity with, this Memorandum of Understanding.
Areas of Responsibility
6.     General Responsibilities. For purposes of implementation of the LGDP, and under the
terms and conditions specified in paragraphs 2 - 5 above, TSC acts on behalf of MLGRI) as the
responsible Sector Ministry. Under those general terms, TSC shall be specifically responsible
for supporting the district assemblies responsible for the towns of Bawku, Bolgatangt. Cape
Coast, Elmina, Ho, Keta, Koforidua, Sunyani, Swedru, Techiman, and Wa by performing the
following functionstactivities with respect to GOG/1DA LGDP investments for waste
management, markets and lorry parks, and streets and road-related drains; as follows:
(a)    Receive investment proposals direaly from the relevant District Assemblies and,
with the assistance of suitably qualified consultants, assess the feasibility of such
proposals (TSC will provide MLGRD with copies of all documentation received
from the District Assemblies and correspondence in this regard between district
assemblies and the TSC);
(b)    Be responsible, on behalf of the specific Dismict Assembly involved, for
supervising consultants responsible for preparing detailed engineering designs for
projects which have been judged technically feasible and are within the scope of
the IDA-financed LGDP - in that regard, TSC will -
(i)   Include the responsible district level engineering officer, where assigned
and available, in the supervision process as a form of on-the-job training;
the modalities of such involvement/training of district engineering
officers to be specified prior to Project Effectiveness (with respect to the
waste management component, the relevant engineer will be staff of the
District Assembly's Waste Management Unit, where such units have
actually been established),
(ii)   With specific respect to the waste management component, will clear the
Terms of Reference for, and technical specifications of, all detailed
engineering designs with the Government of Ghana Supply Commission
(GSC) and the Ministry of Environment (ME). IiQIE: Adoption of
this clause will be subject to any over-riding clauses regarding the role,
if any, of GSC and/or ME which might be included in the GOG/IDA
Credit Agreement.], and
(iii)   With specific respect to the streets and road-related drains component,
will consult with the Ghana Highways Authority (GHA) and or
Department of Urban Roads on the Terms of Reference and technical
specifications of all detailed engineering designs.
(c)    Facilitate approval of financing for approved projects based on formally recorded
"no objections" from the relevant District Assembly, MLGRD, and, where
required by the GOGtlDA Credit Agreement, IDA;
(d)    Maintain, jointly with MLGRD, a Special Account for the holding and
disbursing of IDA funds and a Project Account for the holding and disbursing
COG counterpart funds, authorized signatories for which wiU include at least one

7.    Procurement. TSC's specific responsibilities with regard to procurement, will be to
coordinate, manage, and assure that correct procurement procedures are observed during the
entire project cycle, Inter alia:
(a)   Select and Monitor consultants in the preparation of Bid Packages (with respect
to the Waste Management Component, in consultation with GSC and the relevant
District Assemblies) and review such packages prior to finalization;
(b)   Select and Monitor supervise consultants in the establishment of technical
specifications (as outlined in para. 7[b] above);
(c)    Select and Monitor consultants in the preparation of Bid Documents to be
reviewed by IDA and those GOG agencies as required or appropriate;
(d)   Submit required procurement documents and evaluation reports to IDA as
required;
(e)    Advertising for/sale of/soliciting bids;
(t)   Jointly with the relevant District Assemblies, evaluating bids (with specific
respect to the Waste Management Component, including GSC); and
(g)   Following local approval by GOG, regional, or district tender boards (as
appropriate) and in parallel with local coordion of the procurement process,
supervision by TSC of the procurement process and actual delivery of the
procured goods and services.
S.    Internal tTSC) Personnel Policy and Management. It is assumed here that any
addonal staff which might be assigned to TSC for the specific purpose of implementing LGDP
(i.e., in addition to those already employed by TSC) will be employed under the terms of
Personnel Services contracts and, thus, will not be G(3G Civil Servants. Therefore, the terms
and conditions of service for such staff will be proposed by TSC, approved by MWH and the
Ministry of Finance and Economic Planming (MFEP), and incorporated in individual contracts.
Specific cotact employees will be recruited by TSC, but the actually hiring decision will be
made by a committee consisting of authorized representatives of MLGRD, MWH, MFEP, and
the Public Services Commission (PSC). Promotion and/or transfer decisions will be subject to
the terms and conditions established for those purposes by the individual contracts. However,
in most cases, the same process specified above for original employment decisions will be
employed; in effect promoting or transferring contract personnel requires a new contract.
Authority to dismiss employees contracted specifically under the terms of LGDP will be retained
by the Director of TSC, subject to approval of MLGRD and the standard termination and
arbitration clauses included within employment contracts financed by IDA.
9.    Finally, it should be noted that TSCs responsibility are limited to the investment phase
of the IDA-financed LGDP project and does not extend to the operaions and maintenance phase
which follows completion of the investment phase. In addition, TSC has no ddct responsibility
for implementing the Local Government Capacity-BUiig  component of the project (with the
exception of facilitating the process for any large scale procurement of goods and services for that

revenue policy, revenue collection systems, and/or personnel policy and management.

1.    Monitoring indicators suggested below presuppose the existence of a year-by-year project
work plan which lays out, by quarte (a) the main physical implementation targets and (b) budgetary
expenditure targets. This overall work plan should be updated at least once per year. Monitoring
would involve comparing targets with indicators of actual progress. 1/
2.    Ihe Technical Services Center will be responsible for collecting and processing the
monitoring data and for preparing quarterly progress reports. In some cases, the information will be
directly available from TSC. In other cases, the concerned implementing agency (e.g. MLGRD,
District Assembly) will need to supply the data.
3.    TSC is currently using a system for budgetary reporting developed for the Urban II project
which can continue to be applied. Under the Local Government Development Project, some
additional implementation monitoring indicators will be used, as listed below.
4.    Also, in line with curent World Bank guidelines, monitoring wiUl extend to a number of
simple performance indicators. These refer to the quality of services delivered and institutional
capacity achieved after the inital investments in works, equipment, technical assistance, and trining.

APUrULIc Of GHANA
LOCALF GOVERNN14T DEVELOPMET PROJECT (URBAN III)
"U=gER OF ICA;L GOVEJNTTr DMELOPNEI'OLWCY
The establishment of Ditrict ASsemblies in Ghana from 1988
commenced implementation of the policy of dece..tralization in the
country's public administration. Since then all efforts have been
geared towards pursuing a decentralization programme which would
see a devolution of power and authority with responsibilities for
a wide range of functions from Central Government Agencies to the
District Assemblies accompanied by the means to exercise those
responsibilities at the District or Local Level.   Hence, the
promulgation of the Local Government Law of 1988, PNDC Law 207.
With the promulgation of the Constitution of the 4th Republic of
Ghana in 1992, followed by the proclamation of the 4th Republic on
7th January, 1993, a draft Local Government Bill embodying
amendments to Law 207 has been drafted and has been placed before
Parliament.   In essence the Constitution retains the policy of
decentralization and vests Parliament with powers to promote it.
2.   In the  long term, the policy aims at ultimately  seeing
District Assemblies established as full fledged decentralized
Institutions with sufficient autonomy and adequate resources to
plan, manage and maintain service delivery, and carry out
consistent development in the districts. This implies developing
the capacity of District Assemblies to explore existing and
potential resources to aid operation and maintenance and
development.   It also means that District Assemblies  would
eventually be able to employ and maintain the services of required
staff, particularly professionals like Administrators, Accountants,
Planning  Officers,  Legal  Staff,  Doctors  and  Engineers  on
competitive termo.
3.   In this connection, a commitment has been made in the new
Local Government Act to establish a Local Government Service,
distinct and separate from the Civil service, as part of the Public
Service of Ghana. The Act also provides for the transfer of Civil
Service personnel currently working in the District Departments to
the Local Government Service when established.
4.   The main objective of the projected creation of the Local
Government Service is to implement the constitutional requirement
that " persons in the service of local government shall be subject
to the effective control of local authorities".



-170-                         Annex 20
Page 2 of 5
5.   It is planned to conduct a detailed study of the issues
that need to be addressed to ensure that the Local Government
Service will promote the autonomy of the District Assemblies,
Some of the issues to be examined in the study are:
i.  Conditions of service that will attract the right
calibre of personnel;
ii. Structure and organisation of the Service to ensure
effective management; and control of employees by
and   allegiance  to  the   individual   District
Assemblies;
iii. Affordability in terms of cost of establishing the
Service and also cost to each District Assembly;
iv. Funding arrangements;
v. Incentives by Individual Asaembliea to attract
personnel and the impact of auch arrangement on
recruitment  for  and  by  disadvantaged  District
Assemblies; and
vi. Practices and procedures that would promote
accountability  of  the  staff  to  the  District
Assemblies.
6.   Presently, however:
(a)  The  Civil  Service  Law,  1993,  PNDC  Law  327,  has
transferred 22 Decentralized Departments to the District
Assemblies. They are to cease to operate as line
Departments of ?4inistries and operate essentially as
Departments of the District Assemblies offering technical
and/or professional advice in their respective areas and
implementing policies of the District Assemblies.
In other words, they will constitute the bureaucratic
machinery through which decisions of the District
Assembly will be Implemented and programmes executed.
They will be responsible to the District Assemblies. The
District Assemblies may recruit required additional staff
through the Public services Commission to strengthen the
Departments.
(b)  District Assemblies will begin to assume responsibility
for planning functions (spatialI investment and economic)
in the District as aBsigned to them under the provisions
of the new Local Government Act and within the framework
of the proposed National Development Planning (System)
Act.   A National Development Planning Commission has
already been set up.
(C)  District   Assemblies   will   develop   and   manage
infrastructure and provide essential and needed services
to the Communities.



-171-                        Annex 20
Page 3 of 5
7.   The short term processes and o;WJectives outlined above can be
achieved in the 11 Project Districts with the support of the LGDP
(Urban III) in the following ways:
(i)  District Assemblies Capacity Building:
Thia will involve technical assistance, training and
equipment.   Planning and Budget personnel should be
equipped with the technical knowhow to enable them place
District  Planning  and  Development  in  the  right
perspective* Similarly support is needed for:
( a)   increased revenue generation and collection
(b) improved budgeting and financial management
(c) planning system development and
(d) strengthening of Tochnical Departments of
the progect Districts.
Hopefully the process can be replicated in other
Districts.
(ii) Rehabilitation and Improvement of urban infrastructure
and services. This will consist of:-
(a) rehabilitation of existing District capital
town center roads and associated drains and
traffic management measures
(b) upgrading of existing public markets and motor
parks; and
(c) improvements in solid waste collection and
disposal and in urban sanitation
B.  As far as responsibility of the various levels of government
are concerned the District Assemblies perform:
(a) administrative,  plannlng   and  development
functions at the District level; existing
legislation designates the District Assemblies
as the responsible authorities and assigns
powers for the purpose;
(b)  traditional   or   known   local   authority
functions;  and  transferred   functions  of
Central Government.
These are constituted by the functions of the Decentralized
Departments. Existing legislation specify 86 additional functions
for the District Assemblies. The Sub-District structures of Urban,
Town, Area and zonal councils and Unit Committees will carry
decentralization further down to the very local levels and perform
some stated functiona as well as some assigned functions from the
District Assemblies. In all these, the Metropolitan/Municipal and
District Assemblies should be seen as the highest administrative,
planning and development authorities in their respective areas, to



-172-                        Annex 20
Page 4 of 5
whom all levels of authority in the metropoles/ municipalities and
Districts are responsible.
9.   Considering the fact that District Assemblies are incapable of
carrying out their assigned functions all alone owing to several
factors, including financial constraints, the Constitution provides
for safeguards in inter governmental financial relations. There Is
a specific provision for the establishment of a District Assemblies
Common Fund into which not leos than 5% of total national revenue
is required to be paid for disbursement to the District Assemblies
for development purposes. The Common Fund has been established and
its  Administrator  appointed.   The  fund  is  expected  to  be
operational effective from January 1, 1994.
10. Allocations to the Common Fund will be haaed on revenues
accruing to the Central Government other tha.a foreign loans,
grants, non-tax revenues and revenues already collected by or for
District Assemblies under any national enactment in force. The Act
also provides for Central Government and/or any bodies or persons
to make grants-in-aid to any District Assembly. With these
provisions, District Assemblies will continue to collect their
local  fees  and  rates.  Central  Government  Revenues  ceded  by
legislation to the District Assemblies and collected centrally by
the Internal Revenue Service on their behalf and shared to the
Assemblies by the Ministry of Local Government and Rural
Development are protected for the District Assemblies and will
continue to be disbursed as additional resources to receipts from
the Common Fund.
11. The formula for sharing the Common Fund, to be approved by
Parliament, will however take account of the development status and
the level of local contributions to funding of developments related
to the functions of the District Assembly. District Assemblies will
have discretion to select projects to be funded with their Fund
allocations, on  the basis of district priorities within broad
national policy guidelines. This is to ensure that there are no
disincentives for local revenue collection. Allocations from the
Common Fund shall be used for development and not for recurrent
costs such as salaries and allowances.
12. External Funds in the form of credits and grants are not
specifically provided for in the Act but under existing
arrangements, Government may make such funds available to any
District Assembly (e.g. IDA supported Urban *. Project and the
Urban III Project) to support the District Assemblies and promote
the decentralization process.
13. It is recognised, however, that it is necessary to improve
management at the local level through some incentive measures.
Staff of the right calibre, qualification and experience should be
secured in the first place. For such staff to be willing to ofier
their services In the District Assemblies,  the latter must be



-173-
Annex 20
Page 5 of 5
capable of ongaging them on competitive conditions of service with
regard to salary, career progression and security of tenure. An
important option which is being considered, for A start, in the
transfer of funds from the consolidated fund to cover the salary
payments  of  some  specified  staff  and  require  the  District
Assemblies to rationalise their staff establishments and prepare
them to assume greater reaponsibility in the engagement and
retention of staff In due course. Within the framework of the
Civil Service Reform Programme,   there is scope for improved
personnel management.
14. It is hoped that when Urban III gets underway with the agreed
support, It will set the pace for urban infrastructural development
and   operation   and  maintenance  of  services   in  District
Assemblies.
